## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Pod Eviction on Node Memory Pressure

## Your Task

Pods are evicted with reason 'memory pressure'. Find the Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that (1) define the memory pressure eviction thresholds and (2) implement the eviction manager's decision logic for memory-pressure-based pod eviction.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

I am thinking...: Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the memory pressure eviction system in Kubernetes. Let me summarize the key files:

1. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go`** - Defines the eviction threshold types and signals, including `SignalMemoryAvailable` and `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` which are the memory pressure signals. Also defines `Threshold`, `ThresholdValue`, `ThresholdOperator`, and `OpForSignal`.

2. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go`** - Defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "100Mi"` as the default hard eviction threshold for memory on Linux.

3. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go`** - Defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "500Mi"` for Windows.

4. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_others.go`** - Defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "100Mi"` for other platforms.

5. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go`** - The main eviction manager implementation:
   - `managerImpl` struct - the eviction manager
   - `NewManager` - creates a new eviction manager
   - `synchronize` - the main control loop that enforces eviction thresholds (key decision logic)
   - `IsUnderMemoryPressure` - returns true if node is under memory pressure
   - `Admit` - rejects pods when node is under pressure
   - `evictPod` - actually evicts a pod

6. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go`** - Helper functions:
   - `ParseThresholdConfig` - parses threshold configuration
   - `rankMemoryPressure` - ranks pods for eviction under memory pressure
   - `signalToNodeCondition` - maps `SignalMemoryAvailable` and `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` to `NodeMemoryPressure`
   - `makeSignalObservations` - derives observations for eviction signals
   - `thresholdsMet` - determines which thresholds are met

## Summary

The memory-pressure-based pod eviction system in `kubernetes/kubernetes` (v1.32.0) spans these key files:

### Files Defining Memory Pressure Eviction Thresholds

1. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go`** — Core type definitions:
   - `SignalMemoryAvailable` = `"memory.available"` (node-level memory)
   - `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` = `"allocatableMemory.available"` (pod-allocatable memory)
   - `Threshold` struct with Signal, Operator, Value, GracePeriod, MinReclaim

2. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go`** — `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "100Mi"` (Linux)
3. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go`** — `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "500Mi"` (Windows)
4. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_others.go`** — `DefaultEvictionHard` with `"memory.available": "100Mi"` (other platforms)

### Files Implementing Eviction Decision Logic

5. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go`** — The eviction manager (`managerImpl`):
   - `synchronize` — main control loop that evaluates thresholds and evicts pods
   - `IsUnderMemoryPressure` — checks if `NodeMemoryPressure` condition is active
   - `Admit` — blocks new BestEffort pods under memory pressure
   - `evictPod` — terminates pods with reason "Evicted"

6. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go`** — Supporting logic:
   - `ParseThresholdConfig` — parses `--eviction-hard`/`--eviction-soft` flags
   - `signalToNodeCondition` — maps memory signals → `NodeMemoryPressure`
   - `makeSignalObservations` — reads current memory stats
   - `rankMemoryPressure` — orders pods for eviction (by request excess, priority, then memory usage)

7. **`pkg/kubelet/eviction/types.go`** — `Manager` interface definition

Definitions\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/api/types.go`** defines the core eviction threshold types:\\n- `SignalMemoryAvailable` (\\\"memory.available\\\") \u2014 memory available on the node (capacity minus workingSet)\\n- `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` (\\\"allocatableMemory.available\\\") \u2014 memory available for pod allocation\\n- `Threshold` struct \u2014 holds Signal, Operator, Value (ThresholdValue), GracePeriod, and MinReclaim\\n- `OpForSignal` \u2014 maps both memory signals to `OpLessThan`\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_linux.go`** defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `\\\"memory.available\\\": \\\"100Mi\\\"` as the default hard eviction threshold on Linux.\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_windows.go`** defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `\\\"memory.available\\\": \\\"500Mi\\\"` for Windows (higher because Windows system processes need more memory).\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/defaults_others.go`** defines `DefaultEvictionHard` with `\\\"memory.available\\\": \\\"100Mi\\\"` for other platforms.\\n\\n## Eviction Manager Decision Logic\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/eviction_manager.go`** implements the `managerImpl` struct (the eviction manager):\\n- `NewManager` \u2014 constructs the manager with the parsed threshold config\\n- `synchronize` \u2014 the main control loop: collects signal observations, evaluates which thresholds are met (including grace periods), ranks pods for eviction, and calls `evictPod` on the highest-priority candidate\\n- `IsUnderMemoryPressure` \u2014 returns true if `NodeMemoryPressure` is in the current node conditions\\n- `Admit` \u2014 rejects new BestEffort pods when the node is under memory pressure (unless they tolerate the `node.kubernetes.io/memory-pressure` taint)\\n- `evictPod` \u2014 sets pod phase to Failed with reason \\\"Evicted\\\" and kills the pod\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/helpers.go`** provides the supporting logic:\\n- `ParseThresholdConfig` \u2014 parses `--eviction-hard` / `--eviction-soft` flags into `[]evictionapi.Threshold`; calls `addAllocatableThresholds` to mirror `memory.available` hard thresholds as `allocatableMemory.available`\\n- `signalToNodeCondition` init block \u2014 maps `SignalMemoryAvailable` and `SignalAllocatableMemoryAvailable` to `v1.NodeMemoryPressure`\\n- `makeSignalObservations` \u2014 reads current memory stats from the summary provider to produce signal observations\\n- `rankMemoryPressure` \u2014 sorts pods for eviction under memory pressure: first by whether usage exceeds requests, then by priority, then by memory consumption above requests\\n- `byEvictionPriority.Less` \u2014 ensures memory signals are ranked first among all eviction signals\\n\\n**`pkg/kubelet/eviction/types.go`** defines the `Manager` interface (including `IsUnderMemoryPressure()`) and the `Config` struct that holds the parsed thresholds.\\n\\n## Execution Chain\\n1. At kubelet startup, `ParseThresholdConfig` (helpers.go) converts `--eviction-hard`/`--eviction-soft` flags (e.g., `memory.available<100Mi`) into `[]evictionapi.Threshold`.\\n2. `NewManager` (eviction_manager.go) stores the config and creates the `managerImpl`.\\n3. The `synchronize` loop (eviction_manager.go) runs periodically: it calls `makeSignalObservations` to read current memory levels, evaluates `thresholdsMet`, updates `nodeConditions` (setting `NodeMemoryPressure`), and when thresholds are met calls `rankMemoryPressure` to order pods.\\n4. `evictPod` (eviction_manager.go) terminates the top-ranked pod with reason \\\"Evicted\\\" and message indicating the node was low on memory.\"\n}"
